  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText2553928981950118377" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Blood sings to blood, Froi . . . <br />Those born last will make the first . . . <br />For Charyn will be barren no more.</b>
</i><br /><br />Three years after the curse on Lumatere was lifted, Froi has found his home... Or so he believes...<br /><br />Fiercely loyal to the Queen and Finnikin, Froi has been trained roughly and lovingly by the Guard sworn to protect the royal family, and has learned to control his quick temper. But when he is sent on a secretive mission to the kingdom of Charyn, nothing could have prepared him for what he finds. Here he encounters a damaged people who are not who they seem, and must unravel both the dark bonds of kinship and the mysteries of a half-mad Princess.<br /><br />And in this barren and mysterious place, he will discover that there is a song sleeping in his blood, and though Froi would rather not, the time has come to listen.<br /><br />Gripping and intense, complex and richly imagined, <i>Froi of the Exiles</i> is a dazzling sequel to <i>Finnikin of the Rock</i>, from the internationally best-selling and multi-award-winning author of <i>Looking for Alibrandi</i>, <i>Saving Francesca</i>, <i>On the Jellicoe Road</i> and <i>The Piper's Son</i>.</span>

        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_15798690').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_15798690').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_15798690').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script></div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_139574512" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139574512" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139574512?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763647599" href="/book/show/12154330-froi-of-the-exiles">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=aus-nz">aus-nz</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=3">3</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=starred-2012">starred-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139574512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7598742404400399617">As seen on <a href='http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/02/froi-of-the-exiles-by-melina-marchetta.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Readventurer</a><br/><br/>You know what is sad? That <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_' title='Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Froi of the Exiles</a> is #76 on the Goodreads list of most popular books released this October, while <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10637766.Silence__Hush__Hush___3_' title='Silence (Hush, Hush, #3) by Becca Fitzpatrick' rel='nofollow noopener'>Silence</a> is #1. Will <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta' title='Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melina Marchetta</a> ever get the acknowledgement she deserves? Will her publishers ever promote her books the way they deserve to be promoted? I mean, so much effort and money is put into hyping garbage, why not put it towards something worthy? Very few people I'd recommended this author's novels disliked them, so would it be re</span>
  <span id="freeText7598742404400399617" style="display:none">As seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/02/froi-of-the-exiles-by-melina-marchetta.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a><br /><br />You know what is sad? That <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a> is #76 on the Goodreads list of most popular books released this October, while <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10637766.Silence__Hush__Hush___3_" title="Silence (Hush, Hush, #3) by Becca Fitzpatrick" rel="nofollow noopener">Silence</a> is #1. Will <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta" title="Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Melina Marchetta</a> ever get the acknowledgement she deserves? Will her publishers ever promote her books the way they deserve to be promoted? I mean, so much effort and money is put into hyping garbage, why not put it towards something worthy? Very few people I'd recommended this author's novels disliked them, so would it be really that risky to market them properly? Ok, I think I've reached my ranting quota for the day. Let's talk about something more heartwarming - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a>. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4932435.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles__1_" title="Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles #1) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Finnikin of the Rock</a> was a fine fantasy novel in itself, but I think there is more of everything in its sequel. There is more heartache, more pain, more adventure, more mystery, more secrets, more magic, more intrigue and more madness. <br /><br />Three years after the breaking of the Lumateran curse Froi is sent to neighboring Charyn on a revenge mission. What first is thought to be a simple avenge-and-escape task, quickly becomes something more when Froi learns of a curse hanging over Charyn, a curse that is even more horrifying than the Lumateran one. And the person who seems to suffer the most because of it is the half-mad Princess of Charyn Quintana. Hers is the unbearable and thankless burden to save the country which is about to explode from the inside.<br /><br />Now, I will refrain from saying more about the plot to stay away from inadvertently revealing secrets and plot twists. Trust me, there are many. But I will tease you with a few things: Quintana - she broke my heart, a poor girl who has to serve her land by doing things most degrading; Lucian - I was ashamed of him in the beginning, I was in pain for him in the end; Froi - he has become a man of wondrous strength and depth and he might have met his match - someone of equal passion and darkness of soul. These are only a few familiar characters that took possession of my heart, but there are more, equally fierce and unforgettable - a couple of old men with dark pasts, a defiant whore, a stuttering idiot girl who finds her worth in spite of everyone calling her useless.<br /><br />It won't be a proper <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta" title="Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Melina Marchetta</a> book review if I don't mention how much I cried over it. And, of course, I did quite a bit. I cried because I felt shame and of pity and in triumph.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a> is a huge book. It is so big, I am actually surprised it wasn't split into two, because, if you look at it, the climax of the story happens at about half way point. But for such a lengthy book, it is surprisingly unputdownable and very tightly written.<br /><br />You also need to know that this is only a half of the story. The cliffhanger is big, softened only by a mercifully hopeful epilogue. <br /><br />I remember Marchetta promised not more than a year between publications of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165761.Quintana_of_Charyn__Lumatere_Chronicles___3_" title="Quintana of Charyn (Lumatere Chronicles, #3) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Quintana of Charyn</a>. I sure hope it's true. I foresee this wait to be quite agonizing. <br /><br />P.S. Many have been asking where we got this book released only in Australia at this point. Check here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.fishpondworld.com/Books/advanced_search_result.php?rid=225654465&amp;keywords=melina%20marchetta">http://www.fishpondworld.com/Books/ad...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7598742404400399617" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_214436572" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/214436572" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/214436572?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=fun-fantasy">fun-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=leaves-awesomeness-behind">leaves-awesomeness-behind</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=australian-writer">australian-writer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer214436572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer798745089080618774">Sometimes I feel like Marchetta books should come with a public health warning.<br/><br/>"Marchetta Fever," it would say. <br/><br/>"Symptoms include: pain, aching or burning in the chest region indicating a broken heart.<br/><br/>Uncontrollable weeping, both happy and sad, may occur frequently. More serious cases run the risk of having their mind blown.<br/><br/>This condition has no known cure."<br/><br/>That's me. That's me with every single one of these books. <br/><br/>I went into my local bookstore to order me some Marchetta this year. Let me expla</span>
  <span id="freeText798745089080618774" style="display:none">Sometimes I feel like Marchetta books should come with a public health warning.<br><br>"Marchetta Fever," it would say. <br><br>"Symptoms include: pain, aching or burning in the chest region indicating a broken heart.<br><br>Uncontrollable weeping, both happy and sad, may occur frequently. More serious cases run the risk of having their mind blown.<br><br>This condition has no known cure."<br><br>That's me. That's me with every single one of these books. <br><br>I went into my local bookstore to order me some Marchetta this year. Let me explain the community I live in. The largest shopping center has, I kid you not, FIVE lingerie stores. Stores <i>entirely</i> devoted to selling ladies underwear and such accessories. It has one tiny bookstore. A bookstore that is going out of business. A bookstore that had no fewer than ten copies of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10031701.A_Shore_Thing" title="A Shore Thing by Snooki" rel="nofollow noopener">A Shore Thing</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11349877.Confessions_of_a_Guidette" title="Confessions of a Guidette by Snooki" rel="nofollow noopener">Confessions of a Guidette</a>. Did they have any Marchetta or Laini Taylor? No. One paperback copy of Froi of the Exiles was tucked away somewhere. This is a travesty. This should be considered a Federal Crime. The Unicorn Squad needs to get on that shit and put someone away in the Candy Cane House of Pain for violating awesomeness.<br><br>Marchetta's books are more than just readable, well-written, well-characterized novels of great spirit and imagination. There is a beauty to them, a magic to them which wafts through every sentence of every page. It's not just finely crafted writing, though it is that too. It's a living, beating heart and beautiful but broken soul. <br><br>Does it matter that this book was 600 pages long? Not to me. Not when every page was breath-takingly spectacular. The themes are almost always the same. Loss, pain, healing, family, loyalty. I love the complication and depth of her characterization. <br><br>Whatever it is that Marchetta does, it speaks to me. It touches me in parts of my heart that I had locked away and worked hard to forget. Sometimes it hurts but she always, always remembers to patch me up again when she's finished.<br><br>So, if you're feeling a little lacklustre about your reading selection, why don't you try getting yourself a case of Marchetta fever? It just might be what cures you.<br><br> <br><a href="http://cuddlebuggery.blogspot.com/2011/12/froi-of-exiles-by-melina-marchetta.html" title="This review is also available on my blog" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380335368i/694324.jpg" width="100" height="100" alt="blog link" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="http://soundcloud.com/katkennedy/froi-of-the-exiles-by-melina" title="Audio Review" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380335368i/694326.jpg" width="100" height="100" alt="Audio Review" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>

<div id="review_205973709" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205973709" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/205973709?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763647599" href="/book/show/12154330-froi-of-the-exiles">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer205973709" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18142693882164803138">Once upon a time...<br/><br/>I never would have thought a book could have me sobbing my heart out at four in the morning.<br/>And then <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta' title='Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melina Marchetta</a> wrote <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162022.On_the_Jellicoe_Road' title='On the Jellicoe Road by Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>On the Jellicoe Road</a>.<br/>I never would have thought I'd like traditional fantasy novels.<br/>And then <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta' title='Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melina Marchetta</a> wrote <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4932435.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles___1_' title='Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles, #1) by Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Finnikin of the Rock</a>.<br/>I never would have thought characters could get any better than Finnikin and Isaboe.<br/>And then <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta' title='Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melina Marchetta</a> wrote <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_' title='Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Froi of the Exiles</a>.<br/><br/>I think that if Ms Marchetta were to ever write a bad novel, the earth would simply s</span>
  <span id="freeText18142693882164803138" style="display:none">Once upon a time...<br /><br />I never would have thought a book could have me sobbing my heart out at four in the morning.<br />And then <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta" title="Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Melina Marchetta</a> wrote <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162022.On_the_Jellicoe_Road" title="On the Jellicoe Road by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">On the Jellicoe Road</a>.<br />I never would have thought I'd like traditional fantasy novels.<br />And then <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta" title="Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Melina Marchetta</a> wrote <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4932435.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles___1_" title="Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles, #1) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Finnikin of the Rock</a>.<br />I never would have thought characters could get any better than Finnikin and Isaboe.<br />And then <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta" title="Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Melina Marchetta</a> wrote <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a>.<br /><br />I think that if Ms Marchetta were to ever write a bad novel, the earth would simply slip off its axis and the universe would implode because the natural order of things would have collapsed. Every time I stop and think "THIS IS IT. This is the pinnacle of literary perfection and books just don't get any better than this", Marchetta goes right ahead and releases the proof that I was wrong.<br /><br />This book is just so much better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4932435.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles___1_" title="Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles, #1) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Finnikin of the Rock</a>, and that sounds like I'm insulting the prequel - I'm not. I honestly loved everything about the story of Finnikin and Isaboe. I thought it was a fantastic beginning to this series, both well-written and heart-pounding. But Froi is just more of what I like to read about. Finnikin is a nicer character than Froi; he had many sides to him and was interesting to follow through his adventures, but it was exactly the complications of Froi's character - the battle to control his temper, the struggle to part with the horrors of his past - that made me love him so much more.<br /><br />And Quintana! Oh Quintana, how I'm looking forward to getting more acquainted with you in the next book. I'm not going to spoil this wonderful character for anyone who is yet to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a>, but she is fantastic and weird and I can't wait for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165761.Quintana_of_Charyn__Lumatere_Chronicles___3_" title="Quintana of Charyn (Lumatere Chronicles, #3) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Quintana of Charyn</a>!!!!<br /><br />I love how so many characters came into this book and they all had such distinct personalities. None were wasted and everyone who was introduced had their part to play that was key to the overall story; not a single one will easily be forgotten. Like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_" title="The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Attolia</a> was just so much <i>more</i> than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_" title="The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a>, I felt that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a> was so much more of everything that made <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4932435.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles___1_" title="Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles, #1) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Finnikin of the Rock</a> amazing. It was more exciting, faster-paced, funnier, nastier... even sexier. I got hot flushes at the mention of Froi's "wicked tongue"!<br /><br />I don't really think I can say anything else about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta" title="Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Melina Marchetta</a>. I tend to mention her in most of my reviews because I find her talent for story-telling and creating a variety of complex characters just incredible. She astounds me. How else can I make you Marchetta virgins pick up her work? Let me know and I'll write it in my next review! I hope I've managed to do Froi some justice with this review and that it wasn't just a mess of adoring mushiness. But then, how do you review a perfect book? This is my crappy attempt.<br /><br /><a href="http://emilymay.me" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="18142693882164803138" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_200573833" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/200573833" />
    <a title="Flannery" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/652877-flannery"><img alt="Flannery" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312843258p2/652877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/200573833?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Flannery" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Flannery" href="/user/show/652877-flannery">Flannery</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=young-adult-teen">young-adult-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=swords-and-lasers">swords-and-lasers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=readalong">readalong</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=aussie-ya-is-the-cats-meow">aussie-ya-is-the-cats-meow</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer200573833" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15238134397557831978">I’ve been a fan of every other <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta' title='Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melina Marchetta</a> book I’ve read, which is all of them, so it sort of pains me to say that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_' title='Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Froi of the Exiles</a> was frustrating and unsatisfying for me. I’m still going to give it three stars because even when Marchetta is (subjectively to me) not on her game, she still has a way with words that blows nearly every other YA author out of the water. Originally, I tried to keep my review entirely spoiler-free but it just wasn’t happening. There will be a few spoilers but</span>
  <span id="freeText15238134397557831978" style="display:none">I’ve been a fan of every other <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta" title="Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Melina Marchetta</a> book I’ve read, which is all of them, so it sort of pains me to say that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a> was frustrating and unsatisfying for me. I’m still going to give it three stars because even when Marchetta is (subjectively to me) not on her game, she still has a way with words that blows nearly every other YA author out of the water. Originally, I tried to keep my review entirely spoiler-free but it just wasn’t happening. There will be a few spoilers but they are ones that are not likely to surprise you while reading the book. Oh, and there will be Finnikin spoilers, just so you know. *sigh* And we’re off…<br><br>The number one reason why this book couldn’t work for me was the relationship between Froi and Quintana. It is not a spoiler to reveal something you find out in the first few pages—Quintana has basically been systematically raped for years. While it is happening, she goes off into another place in her mind à la <a>Precious</a> (based on the novel Push by Sapphire) and her daydreams. She has been maltreated for years and everyone thinks she is more or less insane. Also, she is described as having weird teeth, bird’s nest hair, dirty clothes, and several personalities. Okay, so…<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380357327i/708647.png" alt="Quintana" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>How could anyone NOT be attracted to that? All jokes aside, I couldn’t get behind a relationship that disgusted me from the onset. To sleep with a girl who has never had a healthy relationship with anyone, especially if you are doing it under even quasi-false pretenses is a bit scary. I don’t want to call it sexual abuse but it kind of felt that way to me. I know many other readers feel that Quintana is an intriguing character and love her down to the ground. To me, she felt like a confused, somewhat simple-minded girl with lots of strength and motivation but who was absolutely vulnerable nonetheless. I don’t require a strong heroine all the time, that isn’t the issue. The issue is a balanced relationship and here, I just never saw it. Near the end of the novel, Quintana shows immense growth as a character and if I read the third book in the series, I think I will enjoy her more. Froi’s decision to sleep with Quintana was morally questionable. It reminded me of <a>United States of Tara</a> where a woman with multiple personalities and her husband have an agreement that his sleeping with any of her alters is cheating. While her body might be there, her mind isn’t and that isn’t fair to her. Even later in the book, Quintana is randomly growling at points. <br><br>I read a lot of fantasy and romance. In romance novel series, a significant number of authors have a tendency to bring past couples from other books in as characters. Look! See how happy they are! They were happy then but they are even happier now—look at the babies! While I find it annoying, I don’t always mind when this happens in romance books. I <i>do</i> mind when it comes up repeatedly in fantasy and Froi is the only book I can think of as an example. Look at Finnikin and Isaboe! They are so unbelievably well-suited to each other. They are so attracted to each other that they do it up against walls and in closets, tra-la-la! If it were just once or twice, I wouldn’t even note it but it made up a large portion of the novel. On a similar note, I now know another thing that I don’t ever want to read about in another fantasy novel: breastfeeding. How long should someone breastfeed a child? I don’t know nor do I care to think about it while I’m reading a fantasy novel. (unless a woman is breastfeeding dragons or something) Froi of the Exiles was something like 620 pages long. Finnikin and Isaboe had their moment in the limelight in the first book of the series. We certainly could’ve gotten a taste of how sublimely perfect they are together and how they can communicate by looks and how they can’t keep their paws off of each other in a few less pages. <br><br>The tone of this novel is about 400% darker than any of the author’s other work. That’s fine, I don’t mind dark, nor do I mind sex. (in fact, I <i>enjoy</i> these two things in books) A friend told me that Froi seemed more realistic because there was so much emphasis put on the seedier elements of the atmosphere during wartime. Everybody seemed to be either having sex or talking about having sex or if not that, murdering other people. I have no experience living in an active warzone but every character seemed to have sex on the mind, even when they weren’t near any actual fighting. Before you go into this one, you should just know that everyone has slept with everyone else or if they haven’t, they’ve certainly thought about it or are going to in the near future. It got to the point where I just rolled my eyes and skimmed over sections of the book and I never, EVER do that with Marchetta books. (by sections I mean a paragraph here or there, not any significant amount of text)<br><br>I’ve been putting off this review for ages because I just have a bad taste in my mouth about it. I read it with a friend and our google document has over 20,000 words. I am rereading it and laughing because in Chapter 6 my friend wrote, “In general, I am getting more into it. Not a huge fan of travelling around, but looks like they are almost there.” Hahaha, yeah right. There is just so much movement in this book. Everyone is always going somewhere. Just GET THERE already—collect what you came for and go back, or stay. Whatever. I’d understand it if it was like a quest to Mordor to destroy the <i>ring that binds them all</i> but that isn’t the case here. (side note: Turns out I also guessed Froi’s father in Chapter 6 as well) Froi basically spends the entire book moving from one place to the next but I was more interested in his story than the other two storylines that appear in the book. When Finnikin and Isaboe aren’t doing it, they are having political meetings with otherzzzzzzzzz, oh sorry, I just fell asleep while I was typing. The other storyline is about Lucian of the Monts, whom I adored in Finnikin but who has turned into a huge douche in Froi. Let’s say it all together now, COMMUNICATION. Learn it, live it, love it. <br><br>You know what I was thinking about while I was reading? Every one of Melina Marchetta’s books deals with a child with a missing parent. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/82436.Looking_for_Alibrandi" title="Looking for Alibrandi by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Looking for Alibrandi</a>, Josie’s dad is gone but comes back. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162022.On_the_Jellicoe_Road" title="On the Jellicoe Road by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Jellicoe Road</a>, Taylor’s parents are gone and also the guy in the tree side story. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/82434.Saving_Francesca" title="Saving Francesca by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Saving Francesca</a>, her mother is lost to depression. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6407169.Secret_of_the_Seventh_Son" title="Secret of the Seventh Son by Glenn Cooper" rel="nofollow noopener">The Piper’s Son</a>, Tom’s dad was gone to him, and in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4932435.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles__1_" title="Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles #1) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Finnikin of the Rock</a>, he grew up with no mother and was missing his father for years. Now we can add Froi, Quintana, and Lucian to the list. Finding family is a huge theme for her--It’s all about who you are and where you came from. I think this is really interesting but I really enjoy stories about people who don’t know where they are from, DON’T find out, but come to terms with it and become their own person. It is always hard to define yourself when people are pointing out the similarities between you and your parents. I’m not going to spoiler who Froi’s parents are but I saw that one coming down the pipeline pretty early. <br><br>This review is getting too long. I always start to space out after a few paragraphs of a review so I’m assuming I’m not alone in this. I did not truly enjoy the process of reading this book but on the upside, it seems as if almost everyone else did. If you want to know anything else about what I thought of this book, let’s talk about it in the comments. For now, I’m just going to share some more comment highlights I found in our google document (read them at your own risk):<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>“If you are making shadow puppets with someone, it’s safe to say things are getting pretty serious.”<br><br>“And why make out Froi as some legend in the art of tongue work? AWKWARD.”<br><br>“HELLO, people. Wake up and realize that Beatriss needs people to work the land and there are bajillions of Charynites just chillin’ with their vegetable patches and nowhere to go. Problem, meet solution.”<br><br>“ ‘Just ask me! Just ask me! I can’t say the answer without you asking the question!’ Bitch, please. If you can say it when he asks, you can say it anytime.”<br><br>“RAPE.GRAVINAS. STOP PLANTING VEGETABLES!”<br><br>“Everyone’s stories/pasts are so DRAMATIC. This is real, solid DAYS OF OUR LIVES stuff.”<br><br>“I am quick to say, ‘because she is an idiot.’”<br><br>“Everyone’s life sucks. Everything is more convoluted than it should ever be. ALWAYS BE ON THE LOOKOUT FOR A TWIN.”<br><br>“That meeting with the Belegonian dude? <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.snoozefest.com">www.snoozefest.com</a>.”<br><br>“Yes, I noticed that smooth segue.”<br><br>“Why are all the characters such hardened tools? Where is the relaxed, carefree character? Where is MM’s (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/82434.Saving_Francesca" title="Saving Francesca by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Saving Francesca</a>- type) humor? …It is not a relaxing read.”<br><br>“Why is she always growling?”<br><br>“I just love it when guys take my hand and then put it on their crotch.”<br><br>“Maybe Froi and Quintana are somehow brother and sister and it is incest and the little king will come out with extra limbs. Or maybe some cannibalism. You know they’ve been having crop problems. Next step: People eating people.”<br><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="15238134397557831978" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1012960211?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=knots-in-my-stomach">knots-in-my-stomach</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-characters">fave-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=autobuy-authors">autobuy-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-2015-contenders">fave-2015-contenders</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-ya-and-fantasy">fave-ya-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=romance-i-root-for">romance-i-root-for</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1012960211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2544022357384182222"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422393504i/13497860._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>My thoughts after reread</u>
</b> : If there's something this reread taught me, it's that I can't think of a better author than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melina Marchetta</a> to deal with a character as Froi with such honesty, depth, and respect. I won't shy away from the truth : Froi, as a 14 years-old rootless and lawless slave, attempted to rape the MC in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4932435.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles___1_' title='Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles, #1) by Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Finnikin of the Rock</a>, and I will never, ever, condone such awful and criminal behavior. Yet <u>there's where <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melina Marchetta</a>'s brilliance shows itself</u> : <b>giving Froi this book, </b></span>
  <span id="freeText2544022357384182222" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422393504i/13497860._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>My thoughts after reread</u>
</b> : If there's something this reread taught me, it's that I can't think of a better author than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Melina Marchetta</a> to deal with a character as Froi with such honesty, depth, and respect. I won't shy away from the truth : Froi, as a 14 years-old rootless and lawless slave, attempted to rape the MC in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4932435.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles___1_" title="Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles, #1) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Finnikin of the Rock</a>, and I will never, ever, condone such awful and criminal behavior. Yet <u>there's where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Melina Marchetta</a>'s brilliance shows itself</u> : <b>giving Froi this book, she never, ever tries to excuse or simplify his behavior. She doesn't make us love him under false pretenses. She doesn't pretend his actions were inconsequential and more than that, <u>they're never forgotten</u>.</b> She gives him layers, regrets - <i>fears</i>, self-loathing, doubts, and yes, <i>hope</i>. <br><br><b>And doing that, she creates one of the most complex and heartbreaking character I've ever met.</b> I won't deny that. My heart broke for him, beat for him, and I'm not ashamed of my emotions. <br> <br><b>
  <u>Original review</u>
</b> : As you might know, I'm a teacher from 3rd to 5th grade. Of course I love my job but let's face it : <i>sometimes the gremlins are exhausting</i>. <br><br><u>To survive, I learnt quickly a few tips</u> : <br>- Everything is better in color<br>- Sleep full-time nights - or if you don't, pretend, that is to say, <i>smile</i>.<br>- Identify the <i>giggles words</i> and defuse the crisis right away : <i>yes, there is sex in sexism, hahaha, now can we talk about it?</i> Now, you're a teacher but also a person, so try to never forget it and allow you to laugh sometimes. Except at other times. <i>No, we don't eat acorns. Squirrels eat acorns. Pigs eat acorns. You're a ten years old boy <s>dammit</s></i> ← yeah, because you never swear in public.<br>- Protect your voice : no need to yell. Never. <br>- <b>Tool worksheets are your friends, because surprisingly, you're not a parrot.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422393504i/13497861._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Target</b> : To be able to read this book without crying.<br><br>✔ <b>Never underestimate Marchetta's ability to blow your mind</b> : you need to remember that nothing can be taken for granted, neither the characters' reactions because they're dynamic and evolve, nor the curse of the story, because you can't even talk about <i>twists</i> when that's the whole story which is unpredictable. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Most days, he feared that a monster of great baseness lived inside him, fighting to set itself free. Killing the traitors of Lumatere for Isaboe made sense. But killing also fed the monster."</b>
</blockquote><br>✔ <b>Be prepared to fall in love with all the characters, even the villains</b> : indeed in <i>Froi of the Exile</i> none of the characters is annoyingly perfect, and that's fucking great. Moreover, even the word <i>villain</i> seems totally misplaced, because as in life, things are always more complicated than they appeared. <br><br>✘ <b>Froi</b> spends his time fighting between his violent instant-jerk reactions and his self-imposed limitations, and became one of my favorite male-lead of all-time for this exact reason. What could be more interesting than a man who's always seeking his place in the world and who tries to refrain himself without never forgetting who he is? What I adored in his personality is the fact that he's able to see behind the scenes and never hastily judges someone. No, Froi thinks, analyses - and above all that, loves and hates with such passion, <i>craves</i> for some attention - <b>that tortured boy who's trying so hard to be worthy captured my heart <s>and broke it while he was at it</s></b>.<br><br>Do you know what's Marchetta's magic is? <b>She makes me care.</b> So much. Everybody was dismissing Froi, and oh, how I wanted to tear them apart, these cold-hearted bastards! All of them, even those I liked. Even the brothers. <i>All of them.</i> <b>Anything rather than bear his heart-wrenching loneliness a second longer.</b><br><br>✘<b>Quintana</b> fascinated me, but let's face it, the girl is insane. Now, if we scratch the surface, as Froi did <s>did I say how much he's awesome?</s>, we discover one of the most captivating character I've meet for a long time. And if somebody calls her a vessel again I think I'm going to lose it. <i>Fuck off, you jerks.</i><br><br>✘ No need to remember how much Finnikin, Isaboe, Trevanion and Beatriss are multi-layered. No perfection here, just life. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"It's the same with her. Imagine who she would be if we unleashed her onto the world. I think she would rip the breath from all of us."</b>
</blockquote><br>✔ <b>Forget your social life and be prepared to travel, because you're not really in your living-room, nah, you're in Charyn</b>. Indeed if you're like me, you'll probably end completely drawn in this world, enchanted by Marchetta's beautiful words and frowning awkwardly when someone, let's say, your boyfriend, ask you when and what you want to eat. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b> "He says that the gods have forsaken Charyn", Froi said.<br>Arjuro gave a short laugh of disbelief. "The gods have not forsaken Charyn. The gods love Charyn. Where else can they shit, if not Charyn? It's the purpose of this kingdom. To be the place where the gods shit."</b>
</blockquote><br>☛ <u>Crisis management</u> : You answered a phone call. <i>You fool.</i> Okay, fortunately I'm here to help you. So, here's what to do : you <i>hmm hmm</i> a few time, and then you say (intonation is the most important, you play for your life here) : <i>Oh! There's *insert random name of BF/cat/dog/son/daughter/friend* I need to go!</i> And then you hang up quickly. Crisis aborted. Come back to Froi. <i>You're welcome.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"If he was grateful for anything, it was that most times, he did not see their fear. But here in the Citavita, fear made people beg. Fear was piss running down the legs of those who once stood pompus and proud. Fear was a blood-curdling cry that rang through one's ears for days to come."</b>
</blockquote><br>✔ <b>Don't breath.</b> Don't hold your breath though. Or you count. Oh, yes, there's a lot of counting in this book. So let's try this : if your eyes start to be filled with tears, <i>count.</i> Hmmm. I don't know. Try to cope with all the emotions you'll feel, <b>fear, sorrow, hope, sadness, loneliness - love. A love so fierce.</b> Go for a run, share a hug, call your mum. I don't really know. <br><br><i>Oh. My.</i> I think I lied to you : <b>there's no such thing as a potion to avoid crying with this book</b>. Sorry about that. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"And suddenly, in all the absurdity, Froi forgot the orders from his queen. Forgot everything he had been told was right or wrong. Forgot any type of reason."</b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434546074i/15235264._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437141825i/15542036._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_202081123" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/202081123" />
    <a title="Limonessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa"><img alt="Limonessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424025988p2/4147373.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/202081123?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Limonessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Limonessa" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa">Limonessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=australian">australian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer202081123" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5281321059883698487">You know how authors say that once in a story the two main characters get together there is no point in continuing because nobody is interested in reading about them getting married, having babies and discussing about who takes the kids to school? <br/>Well, with Marchetta it doesn't work that way. Because, in fact, in this book she does tell us about the Happily Ever After. She also switches the focus of attention to some OTHER interesting characters and that's where it gets tricky, for the new char</span>
  <span id="freeText5281321059883698487" style="display:none">You know how authors say that once in a story the two main characters get together there is no point in continuing because nobody is interested in reading about them getting married, having babies and discussing about who takes the kids to school? <br />Well, with Marchetta it doesn't work that way. Because, in fact, in this book she does tell us about the Happily Ever After. She also switches the focus of attention to some OTHER interesting characters and that's where it gets tricky, for the new characters have to be unique and <i>interesting</i>.<br />So this is how, in <i>Froi of the Exiles</i> we find all the characters of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4932435.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles__1_" title="Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles #1) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Finnikin of the Rock</a>, especially Finnikin and Isaboe happily together, yet we never get bored. Because this story is mainly about Froi, a <i>trait d'union</i> between our old, well acquainted set of characters and a whole new one, just as amazing as the others and possibly more.<br /><br />The story picks up exactly three years after the events of <i>Finnikin</i>. All is well in the kingdom of Lumatere and people are starting to build new lives for themselves. <br />But it's time for retribution. Froi, who's become an expert assassin trained by the Guard, gets sent to Charyn to kill the King, the real culprit of the curse that's plagued Lumatere for 10 years. <br />Little did the Lumaterans know that Charyn has a curse of its own and Froi is just a pawn in a scheme that goes well beyond the assassination of its King. By meeting Quintana, that half-mad Princess who's believed to be the holder of the key to break the curse, Froi will finally discover his origins and the truth that flows in his own blood. <br /><br />I always forget how Marchetta's books successfully manage to unsettle me every time. It happened with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162022.On_the_Jellicoe_Road" title="On the Jellicoe Road by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Jellicoe</a>, with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7417780.The_Piper_s_Son" title="The Piper's Son by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">The Piper's Son</a> and to be frank, even with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4932435.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles__1_" title="Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles #1) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Finnikin</a>. The stories confuse me at first, their whole force revealing itself well into the narration. So it was for <i>Froi</i>. This book is quite a tome, let me tell you. With more than 600 tightly written pages, it's quite a brick to digest. I don't know how Marchetta managed to keep my attention for so long.<br />Actually, I do. The plot is quite twisted, revelations ensue one after the other and with two story lines going on at the same time, there is no TIME to get bored. The reader constantly travels from Lumatere to Charyn and viceversa, an intelligent strategy in my opinion to keep the story engaging and never dragging.<br />So as my head started to ache for all the court intrigue and politics of the kingdom of Charyn, I was thrown back to some beloved characters of which I knew almost everything there was to know in Lumatere. This is how you digest a 600 and counting page book.<br /><br />The characterization is simply amazing, as usual. Not only we get to know Froi better - and the guy has come a looong way from the street rat we met at the beginning of <i>Finnikin</i> - but the reader will be mesmerized by his sidekicks as well, each and every one well developed and unique. Marchetta manages to make fictional people come alive like no other author does. Quintana is, without a doubt, her greatest success. I loved her. I truly cannot wait for the next book to come out and see more of this amazing creature.<br /><br />And as in <i>Finnikin</i>, the message this book holds within itself is always of outmost importance. Even with the barbarities, the injustices and the abuse that take place within one country, the underlying message contained in the book is undoubtedly one of love and hope. Hope in the generations to come, to learn from the mistakes of the fathers, never to repeat them again:<br /><br /><i>"If your people meant no offence, they should not speak their thoughts out loud in front of their children. Because it will be their children who come to slaughter us one day, all because of the careless words passed down by elders who meant no harm."</i><br /><br />This kind of story, although taking place in a fictional, fantasy world, can truly be valid universally, transcending everything: race, religion, politics, beliefs. It will never grow old and its actuality will resonate for years and years to come. That is how you make a book "immortal", I think. <br /><br />Eagerly, eagerly awaiting the final chapter of this amazing story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5281321059883698487" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_197663915" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/197663915" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/197663915?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763647599" href="/book/show/12154330-froi-of-the-exiles">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=own-a-dtb">own-a-dtb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=amazing-writing">amazing-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2012">reviewed-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=cliffhanger-ending">cliffhanger-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=wonders-from-down-under">wonders-from-down-under</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer197663915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16834721631251052163">Does this book really need another glowing review? A book with 225 reviews on GoodReads alone and 4.62 average rating? What can it possibly change? Maybe not much, but yes, I believe that it does. <br/><br/>Melina Marchetta is extraordinary. Duh. I won’t sing her praise in this review. Almost everyone who ever gave one of her books a chance knows how brilliant she is. Writing about it here seems unnecessary and a little bit silly since it’s the one thing we all agree on, regardless of our favorite among h</span>
  <span id="freeText16834721631251052163" style="display:none">Does this book really need another glowing review? A book with 225 reviews on GoodReads alone and 4.62 average rating? What can it possibly change? Maybe not much, but yes, I believe that it does. <br /><br />Melina Marchetta is extraordinary. Duh. I won’t sing her praise in this review. Almost everyone who ever gave one of her books a chance knows how brilliant she is. Writing about it here seems unnecessary and a little bit silly since it’s the one thing we all agree on, regardless of our favorite among her books or her characters. And that’s just it, there is no doubt about it: we all have plenty to choose from and we love them all, but we all have a favorite – that Melina Marchetta book we simply cannot live without. My favorite is Froi of the Exiles. <br /><br />You can try, if you so wish, to convince me that Froi of the Exiles is not a real person. You can tell me that Finnikin, Perri, Phaedra or Lady Beatriss are all products of someone’s imagination – a brilliant someone perhaps, but just characters nevertheless. You can talk at me until you turn blue, you can offer any number of convincing arguments, you can even bring Melina Marchetta herself to tell me to my face that she made them all up (I doubt she would, though), and I still won’t believe you. Here’s a fact: I’ve never seen my best friend in the flesh, and nobody’s trying to convince me that she’s not real. So why wouldn’t Froi be? I just know that he’s somewhere right now, counting to ten before opening his mouth. <br /><br />The protectiveness I feel towards him after reading “his” book is something I hadn’t anticipated. I went from despising him in Finnikin of the Rock, just tolerating him later on, to loving every little thing about him, the strengths and the many flaws. But I cannot count Froi among my fictional crushes. His story and his raw vulnerability appeal to my maternal instincts and nothing else. (Finnikin is another matter entirely, though, but if I could choose, I’d choose Trevanion.) And in this book, he finally met his match.<br /><br />Where can I even begin with Quintana of Charyn? First of all, who the hell is she? I still don’t know. Isaboe was so easy to love, but Quintana is nothing like her. Where Isaboe is fierce, Quintana is avoidant. Where Isaboe is kind, Quintana is far more likely to bite your head off. But I’m grateful for the difference between them. With this, Marchetta showed that she is perfectly capable of creating not just easily acceptable heroines, worthy of admiration by anyone’s standards, but also unpolished and infinitely crazy girls you’d die for in a second. <br /><br />I won’t lie to you, there were events in this book I was able to predict. But the way they were done, the way secrets were brought to light and my emotional reactions to them exceeded all my expectations. There were parts I had to reread three times in order to fully process them and move on. There were parts where I had to stop for a while and do something else because they were too painful. There were moments that made me laugh out loud and there were parts that left me with my mouth open in sheer and utter amazement. There was a bit of everything, except for a part that left me indifferent. That I have yet to find in one of Marchetta’s books. <br /><br />Now this is where I should write something short and witty to conclude this <s>outburst of admiration</s> review, but I’m drawing a blank. If you live on planet Earth, you’ve probably heard it all anyway. So here’s a useful info instead: the lovely Chachic at <a href="http://chachic.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Chachic’s Book Nook</a> is celebrating Melina Marchetta throughout the week. There are and will be some pretty awesome guest posts, including a not-quite-awesome one by your two favorite nocturnal librarians. <br /><br />Also posted at <a href="http://thenocturnallibrary.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Nocturnal Library</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16834721631251052163" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText11412099294583115345" style="display:none"><b>DNF @pg 165</b><br /><br />Alright, hear me out. I liked the first book but it put me in a slump and I liked this book too, but I've been reading this for like over a week now and I really don't feel it. It isn't the books fault. <div id="review_139579293" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139579293" />
    <a title="Jillian -always aspiring-" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-"><img alt="Jillian -always aspiring-" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393566262p2/3085436.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139579293?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jillian -always aspiring-" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jillian -always aspiring-" href="/user/show/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-">Jillian -always aspiring-</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who likes fantasy with deep meaning, intricate plots, and great characters</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=writer-crush">writer-crush</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=amazing-storytelling">amazing-storytelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=writing-to-which-i-aspire">writing-to-which-i-aspire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=ultimate-favorites">ultimate-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=best-couples">best-couples</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=best-characters">best-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=prose-envy">prose-envy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=wowed-me">wowed-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=heroines-i-love-and-or-admire">heroines-i-love-and-or-admire</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139579293" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5823750957419054148">Authors like Melina Marchetta leave me in an uncomfortable position. As a reader, I'm overjoyed to read books such as hers since they challenge my mind, make me smile and gape alike, and steal away pieces of my heart. As a writer, however, Marchetta's books...<i>intimidate</i> me. Never before have I read work from an author that just keeps getting better and better with each successive novel (and those who have read Marchetta's debut novel, <i>Looking for Alibrandi</i>, know that she has never been even a me</span>
  <span id="freeText5823750957419054148" style="display:none">Authors like Melina Marchetta leave me in an uncomfortable position. As a reader, I'm overjoyed to read books such as hers since they challenge my mind, make me smile and gape alike, and steal away pieces of my heart. As a writer, however, Marchetta's books...<i>intimidate</i> me. Never before have I read work from an author that just keeps getting better and better with each successive novel (and those who have read Marchetta's debut novel, <i>Looking for Alibrandi</i>, know that she has never been even a mediocre writer). I don't know what it is about Marchetta, but it always seems to me as if she is raising the bar higher and higher for herself with each book she writes. It's such an impressive thing that I'm left envious and awed, my writer self and my reader self at war with one another, but one thing is shared between my two halves: the utter respect and admiration for Melina Marchetta as a driving force in young adult literature, whether it be contemporary, fantasy, or any genre she chooses to write.<br /><br /><i>Froi of the Exiles</i>, the sequel to Marchetta's first fantasy novel <i>Finnikin of the Rock</i> and book two of the <i>Lumatere Chronicles</i>, is quite honestly her finest novel to date. The novel is hefty at just about 600 pages, but the pages fly by as you start to read and immerse yourself in the land of Skuldenore with its various kingdoms vying for power, plotting to conquer, or just struggling to survive.<br /><br />The wonderful thing about Marchetta's fantasy writing is that she never loses focus on two key things that are necessary to make any fantasy story succeed: high-stakes intrigues to keep readers captivated and a sense of honest humanity to the world and characters, so much so that readers find themselves empathetic to the characters in both the light and dark moments. Marchetta's "good" characters are just as flawed and conflicted as any villains to be found, adding a very realistic shade of gray to anyone and anything in this fantasy story.<br /><br />No character is more gray than the hero, Froi, first introduced in <i>Finnikin of the Rock</i> as an ex-slave boy who often acted more foe than friend. Though Froi is much reformed when we meet him at the start of this second novel, set three years after the first, there is still a darkness following him, one that he recognizes and fights to keep at bay even as he works for the still-recovering kingdom of Lumatere. But there is something brewing in the kingdom of Charyn, something that may prove deadly for anyone involved with the cursed land...<br /><br />To say that <i>Froi of the Exiles</i> ups the ante from its predecessor is an understatement: Marchetta is in top form with this novel, the threads of the plot seemingly appearing haphazard or inconsequential at first, only to come back later to play in surprising and astounding ways. Nothing is "meaningless" in this novel; everything has its purpose, whether for plot or character development.<br /><br />No matter how tightly plotted, however, this novel would have been a failure if not for the characters -- characters who feel so strongly and so deeply that they feel like flesh-and-blood incarnations simply because their emotions are so palpable. The whole cast of characters are what make this novel so different, so <i>human</i>, compared to stale fantasy worlds and archetypes to be found <i>en masse</i> in hundreds of other novels out there. To be honest, this novel made me want to weep not just for the characters...but because of the plot, the words, the utter talent there must be to craft such an amazing story that holds so much depth and soul to it.<br /><br />This book is a wonderful testament to the fact that truly dedicated and talented authors do not need to be tied by the bounds of genre to create all manner of stories that sing and make readers' hearts ache. For those reasons and more, <i>Froi of the Exiles</i> is definitely the best book I've read in 2011 and one that I would recommend to anyone who wanted a more realistic shade of fantasy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5823750957419054148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1826848619?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L A i N E Y" class="user" itemprop="url" name="L A i N E Y" href="/user/show/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y">L A i N E Y</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
