        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1826848619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16352255770095549429"><b>She, The Ruling Queen Melina Marchetta:</b> What is this thing you all call “second book syndrome” you peasants? I’ve never heard of the term, is it even real? <br/><br/><b>Me, a lowly peasant:</b> Apparently not, your Majesty. Apparently not <br/><br/>——————————————<br/><br/><br/>I feel so <i>satisfied</i>. <br/><br/>That’s the feeling this book gives me. Just so fulfilled and contented - satisfied.<br/><br/>Please, please, <i>please</i> do not ask me how this story is better than others in the same genre, I cannot begin to even attempt to explain why or how or even whatth</span>
  <span id="freeText16352255770095549429" style="display:none"><b>She, The Ruling Queen Melina Marchetta:</b> What is this thing you all call “second book syndrome” you peasants? I’ve never heard of the term, is it even real? <br><br><b>Me, a lowly peasant:</b> Apparently not, your Majesty. Apparently not <br><br>——————————————<br><br><br>I feel so <i>satisfied</i>. <br><br>That’s the feeling this book gives me. Just so fulfilled and contented - satisfied.<br><br>Please, please, <i>please</i> do not ask me how this story is better than others in the same genre, I cannot begin to even attempt to explain why or how or even whatthehell. Just that there was never a moment in this book that I rolled my eyes ever. Was there even info dump in this huge book?? <i>Sagas</i>,I didn’t realize that at all! I enjoyed all of it: the tales, the backstories of every single new character we met. <br><br>ALL OF IT.<br><br>I forgot how hilarious this series can get!! Got a huge flashback to when reading book 1, just <b>incessant laughters. So much so it actually got in the way of my reading!</b> Absolutely fantastic. Uncontainable humor.<br><br>If this was a Regency novel, other characters would be calling Froi ‘a simpleton’ which could carry some derogatory connotation in certain cases but not to me and definitely not with Froi.<br><br>And I just - oh my god - miss that Froi. This is not to say I don’t like Froi in this book. Oh not in the least, but he did feel different to me certainly. Of course it had been 3 full years since the events of the last book and he, along with his fellow travel mates, did some serious character development in our absence. <br><br>Hence came my real disappointment - I would have preferred to bear witness to this so-call growth while it was happening: to see how much he and everyone else struggled and how they overcame each obstacle and ‘be there’ with them. Since Marchetta did a superb job of letting me along the ride with these guys the first time round, I guess I’m addicted to that somehow and still ‘crave’ my share, so to speak.<br><br><br>And that is the ONLY reason I didn’t give this as high rating as the first book. I just infinitely prefer the dynamic between Froi, Finnikin, Evangelin <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Isaboe <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and Captain’s Guards so much more. <br><br>Although the added pov of Lucian’s is such a pleasant surprise and extremely welcomed.<br><br><br>Ps. I still love Lumatere with all of my heart.<br><br><br><br>——————————————<br><br><u>Me finding out the title of the book:</u> <br>Are my eyes deceiving me? Froi?<br>As in Froi <i> my beloved boy who likes playing farmer peasant?</i><br>That Froi?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1480601784ra/21329150.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1765300194" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1765300194" />
    <a title="may ❀" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49148508-may"><img alt="may ❀" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562443036p2/49148508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1765300194?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="may ❀" class="user" itemprop="url" name="may ❀" href="/user/show/49148508-may">may ❀</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

  <u>Why this Book Slays Every Other Book in the World</u>
</b><br/>- froi gets 90% page time<br/>- a princess who is neither beautiful nor sane yet she is still wonderfully f</span>
  <span id="freeText15920260478329320089" style="display:none"><br>Melina Marchetta was gifted with the ability to ruin my life and make me regret everything. I really appreciate it, Ms Marchetta, thank you for that, please never stop. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495599257i/22834686._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> If we forget who we lost,’ Lady Abian would tell Froi and her children, ‘then we forget who we once were, and if we forget who we once were, we lose sight of who we are now.’ </i><br><br><b>
  <u>Why this Book Slays Every Other Book in the World</u>
</b><br>- froi gets 90% page time<br>- a princess who is neither beautiful nor sane yet she is still wonderfully fierce and you cannot NOT love her<br>- ft. so much sass<br>- so many slow burn ships that steal your heart and ruin any other sort of love for you<br>- FINNIKIN AND <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ISABOE AND JASMINA <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> BEING CUTE<br>- SO BLOODY FRICKEN CUTE<br>- I NEED MORE<br>- PLEASE<br>- I’m naming my daughter Jasmina, sorry, its over<br>- ft. craters in my heart<br>- plot twists that chuck your emotions and mental state into a blender and put it on the highest setting<br>- ft. an endless stream of my tears<br>- more plot twists<br>- so much character development<br>- so much world building<br>- so much epic action<br>- so much tears<br>- so much silent compassion and mistakes and flawed characters<br>- the last 5 chapters being better than most books ive ever read in my life<br>- someone hold me please im in so much pain <br>- ft. me not being able to write a real review bc this book has taken over my life and these characters are all I think about <br><br>Actual footage of me rn<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495599257ra/22834685.gif" width="400" height="" alt="description" <div id="review_155158223" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/155158223" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155158223?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=best-of">best-of</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=beloved">beloved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=arc-galley-or-author">arc-galley-or-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=rereading-material">rereading-material</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=male-approved">male-approved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=must-read">must-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=once-upon-a-time">once-upon-a-time</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155158223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17874995283985934202">—————2019<br/><br/>I bow to you, Melina Marchetta! I've read hundreds of books, but none quite as impressive as yours. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/p/BiRH0zoF3Tj/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1558763017i/27567594.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>When I first heard that Froi was going to be the lead character in the sequel to “Finnikin of the Rock” I think I might have given a silent cry inside, as I despised that pitiful young man in (most of) the first book. <br/><br/>Little did I know of the tremendous growth he would go through, the strenghts of his heart and the smarts of his mind, or the power of the song sleeping in his blood. <br/><br/>Li</span>
  <span id="freeText17874995283985934202" style="display:none">—————2019<br><br>I bow to you, Melina Marchetta! I've read hundreds of books, but none quite as impressive as yours. <br><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/p/BiRH0zoF3Tj/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1558763017i/27567594.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>When I first heard that Froi was going to be the lead character in the sequel to “Finnikin of the Rock” I think I might have given a silent cry inside, as I despised that pitiful young man in (most of) the first book. <br><br>Little did I know of the tremendous growth he would go through, the strenghts of his heart and the smarts of his mind, or the power of the song sleeping in his blood. <br><br>Little did I know indeed... Froi did not end up holding only the future of Lumatere in his hands, but also my heart. <br><br>I thought I couldn’t endure more heartbreak after Finnikin’s story ended, but there was so much more anguish to be had in the following book(s). <br>Take one assassin with a past lost in time, one cursed kingdom with a bloodied history, an unwanted princess with a broken mind, a group of people that you can love to hate and love some more. Place them all on a path that will both break and mend their spirits, twist their beliefs and open their deepest wounds. <br><br>And when it all ends don’t hide your tears - when you love so much a story that it makes you shout to the stars, it’s only fair to be overwhealmed by the intensity of your emotions (all that love, too much hate, so much rage, such bittersweet happiness)..<br><br><blockquote>“You keep safe, Froi. Keep safe and come home to us”</blockquote><br><br>It's strange how the turnarounds and the revelations still give me the chills even after re-reading it all these many times, but my love for this story can only grow... <br><br>If you didn’t pick it up yet, I advise you to get your hands on this series and fast. <br><br>————— 2012<br><br>Dear Melina, <br>Keep breaking my heart, because you definitely know the best way to do it.<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melina-marchetta/review-froi-of-the-exiles.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347139i/701494.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="Froi of the exiles" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>Pre-reading thoughts: "If I won't die of happiness, when I'll read this I'll be the happiest person alive :) "</i> Well.. I am the happiest person alive!<br><br>MY THOUGHTS:<br><br>The first story I’ve been told was a fairytale.<br>I don’t remember which one was it, but that shouldn’t be a problem, as they all begin with “<em>once upon a time</em>”, get to the point where the handsome white-horse-riding prince must rescue the princes (falling in love with her beauty at first sigh), and then it ends with a “<em>happily ever after</em>”.<br>All fairytales are about joy, and beauty, and happiness, and the good that conquers it all.<br><br>Too bad this is not a fairytale.<br><br>Too bad we don’t have a beautiful princess, or a charming prince, too bad this is not a story about happiness or happy endings, too bad this is not that kind of story where all the dreams come true.<br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <i>“Is it because we are not beautiful?” she asked.<br>“What?”<br>“That you don’t want to save us. […] In the books of the Ancients the princesses are always beautiful and they always get saved.”</i>
</blockquote><br>This story is about another curse, probably worse than the first one, it’s a story about suffering, and death, and trying too much and losing it all - it will break your heart into pieces, then it will put it back in place only to break it all over again.<br><br>This is a story about a cursed princess and a thief, about wars between kingdoms and assassins, about trust and betrayal, about secrets buried in time and forbidden feelings… This is the story of Froi of the Exiles.<br><br>Let me tell you this: if you loved the first book in the series, you will think that this one is completely insane – but you will love all its madness.<br><br>To be honest, I didn't think a continuation of the story was needed, but damn, now I feel that the story would never be complete without it.<br>Also I must confess that it really blew my mind.<br>There was so much happening, so many new characters to meet, to understand, to distrust, to love, to fear for their safety and to feel the need to cry for their tragic destiny... There was too much pain in this book, too much sadness, to many horrifying memories, too many human monsters, too many heartbreaking scenes, and now there is that need to find what happens next, there is that damned ending that left me hanging, counting the moments until I get the chance to read the next and final book.<br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" height="20" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <i>“If we forget who we lost then we forget who we once were, and if we forget who we once were, we lose sight of who we are now.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>THE CHARACTERS:<br><br><a href="http://gfx-zeus.deviantart.com/art/Assasin-s-Creed-Rampage-273324679" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347139i/701495._SY540_.png" alt="" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Froi</b><br>He is an interesting character, changed from the first book. He is more mature and takes his responsibilities more seriously. His bond with the queen of Lumatere is as strong as before, but his mission is a really difficult one. First because he is all alone, second because he doesn’t know whom to trust, third because he finds new people and he gets attached to them, and this makes his life and his decisions even more difficult.<br>It is hard to love Froi, but it is as harder not to like him.<br>I wanted to punch Froi for holding too much inside his head and heart and for not putting into words all that he really felt, for hurting Quintana so deeply in the beginning, and even after falling for her, for not being able to fight more for her and their feelings, for being weak at times and cruel as well, for knowing how to easily kill the enemy, but even more easily how to break a heart.<br>Still, I cared so much for him and his past, and his deep need to be loved. I wanted to hug him, to take care of him, to change his destiny, to sing for him such that he couldn’t listen to his blood song anymore – maybe, just maybe I could change something in his life, I could bring some joy on his face, I could unbreak a bit his heart.<br>I want him to be happy, I want him to have everything that has been taken away from him since his childhood – I want him next to Quintana, where he belongs.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" height="20" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><i>I’ll come and find you wherever you are. I’ll not stop breathing until I do.</i><br><br><b>Quintana</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" height="20" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><i>Will Quintana of Charyn be beautiful in your play?</i> <br><br>..At least in my review she will:<br><a href="http://folkvangar.deviantart.com/art/Lake-of-Longing-Updated-74023690" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347139i/701496.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Oh, dear Quintana, how much did she suffer for all those people that have never deserved it. All that sacrifice, all that pain, all that shame, all her frustrations and fears – how could someone live with so much pain inside, how could she not lose her mind in such a crazy world? But she didn’t.<br>I wanted to hug Quintana, to take her home with me, to keep her safe, to erase all her bad memories and show her how beautiful the world could be.<br>But in the same time I wanted to cheer for her because she had so much courage and she'd endured so much; because she took the pain of all those last born girls and kept it all inside her; because she suffered for all those people that were supposed to love her; because she has received only coldness and hatred from them all her life and she deserved to be happy.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" height="20" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><i>I heard your song the moment we were born.</i><br><br><b>Gargarin and Arjuro</b><br>These two were such a pair. I loved them as strange as their actions were.<br>I cared for them, for all those horrors they've faced, for all the suffering, for a life full of regrets and no-going-back’s, for a childhood that no one should bear, and for so much more.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" height="20" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><i>If those frescoes could talk they would blush from what they’ve seen the brothers of Abroi get up to in that cave</i><br><br><b>Lirah</b><br>We know by now that we shouldn’t judge someone at first sight. We know by now that Marchetta never creates a character that doesn’t have enough depth. We know by now that all the important characters in Lumatere series have been through Hell and back… this time, literally.<br>Her story was a horrifying as Quintana’s. There are no words to describe her suffering and her loss - for the treatment from her king and his guests, for her baby, for all those years in prison.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" height="20" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><i>Poor Lirah. She’s been imprisoned for at least twelve years, you know.<br>Yes, yes, poor Lirah.</i><br><br><a href="http://scarletvioletta.deviantart.com/art/Commission-for-fromtheskyx-244332617" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347139i/701497._SY540_.png" alt="" width="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Isaboe and Finnikin</b><br>I liked how strong and confident Finnikin has become, and (still) how wise and caring Isaboe showed to be (as much as the situations allowed her).<br>I liked how they fought for the safety of their home and kingdom, but how they wanted nothing more but peace, how they cared about Froi, how they struggled to keep a happy family in all this madness.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" height="20" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><i>'Don't ever ask me again if I hate living anywhere with you and Jasmina. This Rock reminds me of the boy I was and being with you in the palace reminds me of the man I want to be.'<br>'Not just any man,' she whispered. 'A King. Mine.'</i><br><br><b>Beatrice and Trevanion </b><br>I didn't think her story could be more heartbreaking, but it was. I thought her romance with Trevanion would have a quick resolution and a happy ending, but the was more to her story, more hearts to break, more tears to shed for her and her past.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" height="20" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><i>I still wake with your name on my lips every morning</i><br><br><b>Lucian and Phaedra.</b><br>I didn't pay much attention to them at the beginning, but I got to care so much for Phaedra. It broke my heart, it really did. She got from being some minor character to a quite important one, and I got attached to her suffering. She tried too much to be part of a community that resented her, part of a family that didn’t want her, and she had so much to give. I wanted so badly to see them both happy, as they deserved it so much.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" height="20" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><i>If your people mean no offense, they should not speak their thoughts out loud in front of their children, Tesadora. Because it will be their children who come to slaughter us one day, all because of the careless words passed down by their elders who meant no harm.</i><br><br><b>Rafuel</b><br>I am still wondering about this one. I think there is more to him that we could find in this book and I can’t wait to see his part in the next one. All you need to know for now is that he's the reason Froi went to Charyn, somehow he is the key to the past.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" height="20" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><i>“Do you expect me to have regrets?” he asked. “When it’s you Lumaterans who speak an unwritten law that makes the most sense to me.”<br>“And what is that, Charynite?”Tesadora asked.<br>“What needs to be done”</i><br><br><b>The last-born boys</b><br>All I can say about them is that they were really cute and innocent. Protected as they were, they didn’t know much about fights and war, but they meant good – some times that helped, some times it didn’t.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" height="20" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><i>Grijo looked shamefaced. Oliver pretended to. Froi’s head was spinning too hard for anything to make sense.</i><br><br>CONCLUSION:<br>I am conflicted now, because I couldn't believe those horrors, I couldn't bear them.. There was too much pain, too many cries in the wind, to many broken hearts and lives destroyed in an instant. It was horrible and beautiful in the same time - I wanted to scream of frustration, I wanted to take care of those lost souls, I wanted to give them something to hold on to, because without a purpose I don't know how could they survive all that carnage, all those horrors through all those years.<br><br>....Mirror, mirror on the wall, who is the best writer of them all?<br>Melina Marchetta, off course :)<br><br><i>Book source: ARC from the publisher via NetGalley - Thank you so very much!!!</i><br><br><b>Later edit:<br>Check out my <a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/_dreaming-after-midnight/dreaming-after-midnight-8-froi.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Boyfriend #8 - Froi</a><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/_dreaming-after-midnight/dreaming-after-midnight-8-froi.html" rel="nofollow noopener"><span>[image error]</span></a></b><br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melina-marchetta/review-froi-of-the-exiles.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380313075i/688704.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>This review can also be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melina-marchetta/review-froi-of-the-exiles.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a></i><br><br>--<br><br>Later edit:<br>Re-read May 2013 - I might write soon a new review for the series, as it blew my mind once more and I still love it to pieces. Just know that this is a heartbreaking story that I will always hold close to my heart. Absolutely fabulous!!!<br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________</span>

<div id="review_197661031" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/197661031" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/197661031?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer197661031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3896574468498124149"><b>
  <i>"....and he wanted to creep inside her head and join the madness."</i>
</b><br/><br/><br/>So I guess I’m <i>kinda</i> a fantasy fan. <br/>(But still very much a learner)<br/>Because there have now been <i>two</i> series I can’t get enough of<br/>And it’s all to do with Double M and Ms Whalen Turner. <br/><br/>It’s taken me a while to process this book<br/>(Once I got over the jittery caffeine shakes and stiffness of the joints)<br/>Because when I skimmed through my notes I found with dismay<br/>My pages full of only sad faces and exclamation points. <br/><br/>I picked it up wit</span>
  <span id="freeText3896574468498124149" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"....and he wanted to creep inside her head and join the madness."</i>
</b><br><br><br>So I guess I’m <i>kinda</i> a fantasy fan. <br>(But still very much a learner)<br>Because there have now been <i>two</i> series I can’t get enough of<br>And it’s all to do with Double M and Ms Whalen Turner. <br><br>It’s taken me a while to process this book<br>(Once I got over the jittery caffeine shakes and stiffness of the joints)<br>Because when I skimmed through my notes I found with dismay<br>My pages full of only sad faces and exclamation points. <br><br>I picked it up with the intention of spending a few days completely<br>Immersed… but I must admit I failed.<br>For I realised when I had found myself, in awe, at the end<br>That Froi of the Exiles had been accidentally inhaled. <br><br>So due to the fact that my pages are bare<br>And seeing as I read this book in a day, <br>I realised that when it comes to my review<br>I’m probably not going to really have anything to say. <br><br>So if you are looking for advice on whether to read this story<br>Please read the other reviews with more valuable things to add.<br>But like it often happens when you finish an amazing book, <br>I can’t help but feel impossibly sad. <br><br>Because gone is Froi; all fierce and lost, <br>Who counts in his head to prevent his feelings breaking through. <br>With his strength, his passion and his fierce protection.<br>And umm, <i>I guess</i> his shoulders are nice to look at….<br>Especially with that tattoo.<br>*cough*<br><br>And gone is Quintana; <i>“all snorts and giggles” </i><br>Who truly has the ability to <i>“rip the breath from us all”.</i><br>With her squinting and her wonky teeth. <br><i>“The girl who could make rabbits appear on walls”.</i><br><br>But this isn’t just a story about these tragic kids.<br>(But my heart was completely shattered by Queen Q and her Froi)<br>It’s about finding to whom your blood sings, belonging and<br>Broken spirits to be mended. About understanding and of joy. <br><br>(An added note: I can’t help but think that Jo of Mancunia would be<br><s>Lovers</s> <s>Soulmates </s><s>Swivening partners </s><br><i>Strictly platonic</i> with Lucian of the Monts.)<br>And I know I’ll sound impatient with what I say next,<br>But I like what I like and I know what I want...s.<br><br>And what I want is to spend 2012 scowling at the screen<br>Willing that the date for Q of C will get nearer.<br>Because how is it fair (especially with <i>that</i> end)<br>To make us wait another year....er?<br><br>ps.<br>Dear Double M, I would like to suggest that if you ever find yourself<br>On British shores that you should come and give Manchester a look,<br>We have <s>rain</s> <s>football</s> the best music and friendly people<br><s>And me to ask you about the release date of your Jimmy book.</s><br>And me to ask you intelligent questions about this glorious book. <br><br><br><b>Theme Tune.</b><br><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7ZMra7Zyy8o" rel="nofollow noopener">Bat's Mouth by Bat For Lashes.</a> <br><br>Also, I can't believe Double M based some of her research on Conwy Castle! Conwy is one of my favourite places in the world...if you ignore the dive-bombing seagulls, which is difficult when they're trying to nab your chips.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380356736i/708185._SX540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I wonder whether she visited Conwy at the same time as I did.<br>I was the one making my friend stand in the middle of the road so they could get a good picture of me standing with the plastic knight....<br><br>*ahem*<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3896574468498124149" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone with a Heart</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with">chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=o-captain-my-captain">o-captain-my-captain</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=super-sidekicks">super-sidekicks</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer792825180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5225209039863603251"><b>Buddy Read/Re-read with a great group of people at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-lumatere-chronicles-group-read' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lumatere Chronicles Group Read</a></b><br/><br/><b>Second Read Review Dec 23 2014</b><br/><br/>This Book…..This Book. It has all of the emotions in it. I went from <br/><a href='http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/laughing_zpsuymdvpha.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419354336ra/13044694.gif' alt=' photo laughing_zpsuymdvpha.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>to</b><br/><a href='http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/c_zps3a420c16.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393818209ra/8768498.gif' alt=' photo c_zps3a420c16.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>AND OMG QUINTANA</b><br/><a href='http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/hug_zps43161f2d.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419354336i/13044695.jpg' alt=' photo hug_zps43161f2d.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“Because I remembered your words,” she said quietly. “I remembered that you liked me least. You said it in my palace chamber. ‘Have one of the others wake me, for I like you least.’” <br/>She turned to face him and brushed tears fiercely from her face. “Sometimes when I see what’s left of Qu</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText5225209039863603251" style="display:none"><b>Buddy Read/Re-read with a great group of people at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-lumatere-chronicles-group-read" rel="nofollow noopener">Lumatere Chronicles Group Read</a></b><br><br><b>Second Read Review Dec 23 2014</b><br><br>This Book…..This Book. It has all of the emotions in it. I went from <br><a href="http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/laughing_zpsuymdvpha.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419354336ra/13044694.gif" alt=" photo laughing_zpsuymdvpha.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>to</b><br><a href="http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/c_zps3a420c16.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393818209ra/8768498.gif" alt=" photo c_zps3a420c16.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>AND OMG QUINTANA</b><br><a href="http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/hug_zps43161f2d.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419354336i/13044695.jpg" alt=" photo hug_zps43161f2d.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Because I remembered your words,” she said quietly. “I remembered that you liked me least. You said it in my palace chamber. ‘Have one of the others wake me, for I like you least.’” <br>She turned to face him and brushed tears fiercely from her face. “Sometimes when I see what’s left of Quintana of Charyn through my own eyes, I think I can learn to love her. But when I see her through your eyes, I despise her.” <br>If she saw Quintana of Charyn through Froi’s eyes, he knew she’d see a part of himself.</i>
</blockquote><br>This is my second time reading this book and I got so much more out of it. So many more feelings and moments that stole my breath and thoughts away. Marchetta is a genius story teller she broke my heart, she made me hope, I fell in love with so many characters. I have ~250 highlights in this book now and I reread them all and felt this book all over again. <br><br>Finnikin was good but Froi of the Exiles is so much better that I can’t even explain my love for it adequately. I’m so happy I reread it and I’m sure I’ll read it again.<br><br><br><br><b>Original Review Dec 28 2013</b><br><br>Sometimes I ask myself what the secret formula is to writing a great fantasy novel and I think of all of the ones I love the most and for me it is the layers. The best stories have overlapping layers to the characters, plots, arcs, histories and worlds. <b>Melina Marchetta is a weaver of those layers until there is a seamless work of art</b>.<br><br>I was afraid that we would leave Finnikin and Isaboe behind on this new journey with Froi but I was happily surprised that the characters I loved from the first book are all over in this one as well. We join them three years after Finnikin of the rock where we see that Isaboe and Finnikin have been busy indeed. Presented with a great opportunity to get revenge against the King of Charyn, Froi is sent to the palace to assassinate him. But Froi is not who he thinks he is and the princess is not at all what he expected. That is when it all gets confusing. Should he follow the orders of his bond to Lumatere and the Queen, is he the one destined to break the curse that has been placed on all of Charyn or is there another purpose for him still?<br><br><b>
  <i>”In a kinder world,” he whispered, “one I promise you I’ve seen, men and women flirt and dance and love with only the fear of what it would mean without the other in their lives.”</i>
</b><br><br>I think the greatest gift that Isaboe and Finnikin gave Froi is that they showed him that kinder world so that he could see the potential for good in people. When first meeting Quintana it seems that she is stark raving mad, but she is a survivor and somehow she calls to him in a way he never expected. I loved their half crazed talk and how Quintana saw the world. Her story is completely tragic and broke my heart a little (who am I kidding she crushed my heart). After hating Charyn in Finnikin of the Rock for the turmoil they caused in Lumatere for Isaboe and her family it made me hate only the king and not his daughter who was as much a prisoner as anyone in Lumatere.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Until three years ago, I couldn’t read and write, I couldn’t ride a horse or shoot an arrow and didn’t know the difference between a turnip seed and grain. The men who have taught me everything back home, they often say to me, ‘Froi, what if all your talents were left undiscovered?’”<br>He looked up at them. “It’s the same with her. Imagine who she would be if we unleashed her onto the world. I think she would rip the breath from all of us.”</i>
</b><br><br>Quintana is such a complex character and seeing her through Froi’s eyes and how he picks out the sections of her is amazingly written. The backstory for this is huge and so intricate that it could be an entire series all on its own. I don’t want to give much of that away as the pieces were doled out perfectly. I only guessed part of Froi’s true identity everything else well all I can say was I was <b>WOWed</b> by the complexity and brilliance of it. <br><br><b>There are great epic loves, tragedy, hope, sacrifices and every other situation that will tug at your heart and make you love this world.</b> I was so drawn in I cried at parts and laughed out loud at others. There is a great balance so that you are not overwhelmed by some of the horrors told throughout.<br><br><b>Warning:</b> This ends with a few cliffies so have Quintana of Charyn ready to go because you will want to dive right in. Also even though it is categorized Young Adult (YA), some of the situations and content are probably better suited to the upper end of that spectrum and I would say that this is probably good for 15-16+ <br><br><b>
  <u>I can’t say enough how much I loved this series.</u>
</b> <br><br><br>Dec 27, 2013<br>I can not write a review right now because I have to read the next book asap. I will give this more time to review once I'm done with the series....Can I just say WOW-Freaking-WOW-WOW.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5225209039863603251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=e-arc">e-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2-am-or-later">2-am-or-later</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=omg-that-ending">omg-that-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=candlewick">candlewick</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=mind-blowing-good">mind-blowing-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2012-favs">2012-favs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=awesome">awesome</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer236855387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6544107617037565030"><br/>Once again I find myself at a loss for words and I do believe I'm suffering from Marchetta Fever. If you've read any book by her, you may know the symptoms yourself: First it's the euphoria that sets in right after you complete the book. Then, you find yourself thinking about the book long after you finish. You have the inability to form a single, coherent thought to review the book. And in the final stages, your palms go sweaty with the need for the next book. There is a reason why Marchetta is</span>
  <span id="freeText6544107617037565030" style="display:none"><br />Once again I find myself at a loss for words and I do believe I'm suffering from Marchetta Fever. If you've read any book by her, you may know the symptoms yourself: First it's the euphoria that sets in right after you complete the book. Then, you find yourself thinking about the book long after you finish. You have the inability to form a single, coherent thought to review the book. And in the final stages, your palms go sweaty with the need for the next book. There is a reason why Marchetta is considered a master storyteller and if that wasn't evident enough for me in <em>Finnikin of the Rock,</em> then it's now blatantly obvious.  <br /><br /><em>Froi of the Exiles</em> takes place a few years after <em>Finnikin of the Rock's</em> conclusion and is told from Froi's point of view. At first, I was leery of that fact because I really disliked Froi in <em>Finnikin </em>due to the rape attempt on Isaboe. How do you redeem a character that was once viewed as a monster? I didn't know if it were possible to pull it off or pull it off <em>well,</em> but I was wrong. Froi has come a long way since <em>Finnikin</em> and I think the other character's views on Froi really played a big part in my ability to connect with him. For example, we learn in the beginning that he's made a bond with Isaboe to never take another woman by force. Yet, he goes further and says he <em>never</em> will take a woman because he doesn't trust himself. With each chapter, I saw Froi battling his inner demons. But what's even more interesting is that, for me, Froi's redemption came through Quintana's characterization. Because, for Froi, Quintana is the product of what his actions could have created and at the same time falling in love with this very broken girl. I could go on and on about that dynamic, but I'll suffice to say that the character growth in <em>Froi of the Exiles</em> is phenomenal.<br /><br />The plotting was nothing short of sheer brilliance. I've said this before, but the only other author that I find comparable to this level of plotting is J.K. Rowling. While I did find the pacing slower than <em>Finnikin,</em> there were so many twists and revelations that kept me on the edge of my seat. We learn more about Froi's past and I'm still blown how it all came together. There is simply no way to predict anything in this novel. And sometimes I feel like with being an avid reader, you get to the point where you start recognizing certain plot trends and twists. So by the time something is being revealed, it doesn't really shock you. But not with Marchetta. Her plot was woven so thick, I had to take it in piece by piece.<br /><br />By the end of the novel, I felt the same as I did with <em>Finnikin.</em> I felt like I had gone on such an intense emotional journey because so many events had taken place and I needed time to process everything. I loved everything about this book and though, right after finishing I hungered for <em>Quintana of Charyn,</em> I knew I simply couldn't read <em>The Lumatere Chronicles</em> back to back. I'll need to take a mini break before I dive into the conclusion that is sure to turn me into a swirling vortex of emotions. And that, in my humble opinion, is the true mark of a fantastic series.<br /><br /><em>ARC was provided by the publisher via NetGalley. (I'm just really late in getting to it.)</em><br /><br />More reviews and other fantastical things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6544107617037565030" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_156897537" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156897537" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156897537?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156897537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9953473802232011094">I always have a hard time reviewing these books: the ones that aren’t read so much as frantically consumed in a whirlwind of gluttonous book hedonism. Afterward I feel like, <i>“What just <i>happened</i> to me? Yesterday is such a blur…a happy, sad, angry, intense blur.”</i> So, I’ll just apologize now, because this review probably won’t be very coherent.<br/><br/>This book begins like a lot of Melina Marchetta books. (In fact, I might say that <i>all</i> of her best books begin this way.) There’s a mad jumble of names, event</span>
  <span id="freeText9953473802232011094" style="display:none">I always have a hard time reviewing these books: the ones that aren’t read so much as frantically consumed in a whirlwind of gluttonous book hedonism. Afterward I feel like, <i>“What just <i>happened</i> to me? Yesterday is such a blur…a happy, sad, angry, intense blur.”</i> So, I’ll just apologize now, because this review probably won’t be very coherent.<br /><br />This book begins like a lot of Melina Marchetta books. (In fact, I might say that <i>all</i> of her best books begin this way.) There’s a mad jumble of names, events, and relationships spilled out in the first few chapters; it feels like not only a map (which is helpfully provided) but a family tree and a flow chart of some kind might be necessary to keep track of it all. It’s confusing. But, I am not some greenie; I am a Melina Marchetta veteran! I know by now to just keep reading. Sure enough, everything becomes clear (not to mention, extremely engrossing) in no time at all.<br /><br />This book claims on the outside to be about Froi: the young thief and exile who becomes a dedicated Lumateran in <u>Finnikin of the Rock.</u> And there’s no doubt that it is. But of course, we can count on Melina Marchetta for so much more than that. Every one of her books has a complete cast of consuming, vibrant characters and this book is no exception. This book is written in third person but shifts between the perspectives of four different relationships. So, as Froi takes up a dangerous errand and heads into Charyn, the notorious kingdom that once invaded Lumatere and incited a horrible curse, we also get to keep up with all his surrogate family left behind. For all of the <u>Finnikin of the Rock</u> fans out there: rejoice! You’ll get plenty of time with Finnikin, Isaboe, Lucian, Lady Beatriss, Trevanion, Tesadora, and…Jasmina. I’m not going to tell you who that last one is; you’ll have to read this to find out!<br /><br />I don’t even know where to start on the major themes of this book. In a way, this book is about the many facets of romance: infatuation, lust, companionship, love, betrayal, understanding, redemption. It’s also about identity, family, war, hatred, curses, misunderstandings, history, and perspectives. This is one hefty book and I’m not just referring to its massive size. <br /><br />There were so many times where I thought, “<i>No…she wouldn’t….</i>” But OF COURSE she would. There were also times that I assumed dark and dreadful things and she surprised me with lightness and grace. Everything that she writes just feels so true to life. Life isn’t tragic and dark and it’s not easy and wonderful either, but it is both of these at once. People aren’t just greedy or just good or just anything. A whore can be a mother, a severely damaged girl can be a born ruler, an outcast can be a diplomat, a once violent boy can be a healer of women, and an “evil” kingdom is much more than the sum of its parts. <br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />TV on the Radio – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=RMv_PuGHSGA" rel="nofollow noopener">Family Tree</a><br /><br />This song is about dark history, both inherited and remembered. I think that it’s also about how hatred can be fed and perpetuated across generations, but I think that it has a hopeful note too.<br /><br /><i>”Were laying in the shadow of your family tree<br />Your haunted heart and me<br />Brought down by an old idea whose time has come<br />And in the shadow of the gallows of your family tree<br />There's a hundred hearts soar free<br />Pumping blood to the roots of evil to keep it young”</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9953473802232011094" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1980668618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1980668618" />
    <a title="prag ♻" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29249069-prag"><img alt="prag ♻" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598781220p2/29249069.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1980668618?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="prag ♻" class="user" itemprop="url" name="prag ♻" href="/user/show/29249069-prag">prag ♻</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763647599" href="/book/show/12154330-froi-of-the-exiles">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29249069-prag?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29249069-prag?shelf=prose-excellence">prose-excellence</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29249069-prag?shelf=deserves-a-shrine">deserves-a-shrine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29249069-prag?shelf=favorite-pre-2018">favorite-pre-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29249069-prag?shelf=fucked-me-up">fucked-me-up</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29249069-prag?shelf=yam">yam</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29249069-prag?shelf=lgbtqiap-plus">lgbtqiap-plus</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29249069-prag?shelf=okay-fine-i-cried">okay-fine-i-cried</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1980668618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16181165404109510277"><b>One day, I want to do something as well as Melina Marchetta writes.</b> I want to be able to build something even <i>half</i> as emotionally charming as this book. Books like these make me want to put my hardest into everything I do, because these characters and their stories <b>touched me</b> like nothing else has done in a long time.<br/><br/><b>This.</b> This is the real deal. This is literature. <b>This is the kind of book that you will stay up past midnight for and not regret it.</b> This is the kind of book that will make you <i>thin</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16181165404109510277" style="display:none"><b>One day, I want to do something as well as Melina Marchetta writes.</b> I want to be able to build something even <i>half</i> as emotionally charming as this book. Books like these make me want to put my hardest into everything I do, because these characters and their stories <b>touched me</b> like nothing else has done in a long time.<br /><br /><b>This.</b> This is the real deal. This is literature. <b>This is the kind of book that you will stay up past midnight for and not regret it.</b> This is the kind of book that will make you <i>think, feel,</i> and <i>sob.</i> After this book, I get it. I get why people read fantasy and why it’s actually kind of awesome.<br /><br />There are only three things you must know before you start this book, the first being that <b>you must not question Marchetta’s genius, even if you don’t like the book until about 35%</b>. Not a single word Marchetta writes is irrelevant. Not a single preposition, not a single letter is there just to fill up space or provide fluff. <b>Every sentence is impactful and heart-pounding and it will leave you crying with outrage, while at the same time hungry for more.</b> Dialogue you think is filler will turn out to be the climax of the plot seven chapters later. The ending will make you scream because you finally understand the prologue. <b>It’s really not a book you can skim.</b> (And probably not the book for you if you feel like skimming it.)<br /><br />Second: <b>the characters have so <i>much</i> depth.</b> Remember Froi from book one? The scrawny asshole who tried to rape Evanjalin in Sarnak. Well, he’s the main character. But, <i>Sagra,</i> he goes through so much character development you start to love him. Not forgiving him — never forgiving him, but learning <i>with</i> him how his goodness can overcome his baseness.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Until three years ago, I couldn’t read and write, I couldn’t ride a horse or shoot an arrow and didn’t know the difference between a turnip seed and grain. The men who have taught me everything back home, they often say to me, ‘Froi, what if all your talents were left undiscovered?’<br /><br />He looked up at them. "It’s the same with her. Imagine who she would be if we unleashed her onto the world. I think she would rip the breath from all of us.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Lastly, all you really need to know before you go into this is that <b>it’s going to make you so damn emotional.</b> You really won’t understand till you’ve been through it — till about 40% in, I really didn’t care about anybody and I DNFed this book twice. But once you read further, these strangers become characters you would die protecting.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Not exactly what I would suggest, 'Gargarin said. 'It would help if this kingdom didn't see us as a family of savages.' There was silence after that. It was too strange a word for Gargarin to use. <b>Family.</b></i>
</blockquote><br /><br />You guys, <b>read this book.</b> Read it for the characters — read it for the mad princess and the warrior and the gay priestling and the broken architect and Serker's whore and the lost spirits.<br /><br /><b> ⮕ ➡ Shoutout to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508" rel="nofollow noopener">May</a> for forcing this book on me (I can't believe I'm changing the shelves on this from absolutue-crap to this-is-how-you-write-a-book)</b> (This was the best deal ever we're always making more do you hear me)</span>
  <a data-text-id="16181165404109510277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_290669158" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/290669158" />
    <a title="Reynje" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje"><img alt="Reynje" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473722441p2/5590906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/290669158?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reynje" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reynje" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje">Reynje</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer290669158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer303428876887408215">(Scroll down if you'd prefer the<b> tl;dr</b> version)<br/><br/>If <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/402092330' rel='nofollow noopener'>Finnikin of the Rock</a> was a story about a divided and displaced nation’s journey towards healing their collective psyche, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_' title='Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Froi of the Exiles</a> is about a people broken apart by hatred, the wound in their history left to fester, and seep suspicion and fear into the cracks between them. A faceless, malevolent presence in Finnikin of the Rock, this is Charyn’s unveiling as more than simply “the enemy” of Lumatere. It’s an insight into a land burdened b</span>
  <span id="freeText303428876887408215" style="display:none">(Scroll down if you'd prefer the<b> tl;dr</b> version)<br /><br />If <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/402092330" rel="nofollow noopener">Finnikin of the Rock</a> was a story about a divided and displaced nation’s journey towards healing their collective psyche, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a> is about a people broken apart by hatred, the wound in their history left to fester, and seep suspicion and fear into the cracks between them. A faceless, malevolent presence in Finnikin of the Rock, this is Charyn’s unveiling as more than simply “the enemy” of Lumatere. It’s an insight into a land burdened by suffering and grief, and the darker side of human nature. <br /> <br />While Finnikin of the Rock covered more ground in one sense of the word, with a quest that lead its characters into the far corners of Skuldenore, Froi of the Exiles is a novel on a vaster scale in several ways. This story is more complex, with an intricate web of a plot, and it unfolds new dimensions to Marchetta’s fantasy world and the resident characters. Froi of the Exiles plumbs depths of the world only hinted at in Finnikin of the Rock: the detail is richer, each small element is vital and serves a larger purpose in the whole. The themes are pushed further, and by extension the characters are more nuanced, forced to develop in often unexpected, yet organic, ways.<br /> <br />Given the serpentine nature of the plot and the level of intrigue present, at times this is a difficult story to keep hold of. It twists sharply, resists being pinned down, turns in surprising directions. Yet it never feels loose or uncontrolled. There was always a sense, as I read, that Marchetta was driving this story exactly where it needed to go, regardless of how difficult a course she charted. The entire story is characterised by a sense of weight and momentum, that it’s being inexorably drawn to some powerful, inevitable conclusion.<br /> <br />This is an extraordinarily strong book, and probably one I’ll have to read again to fully appreciate the intricacies of the plot, but I believe that its greatest power lies (as with Finnikin) in the characterisation and relationships. Marchetta does not go easy on her characters, providing them with convenient justifications for their actions or plot developments that open up handy loopholes. Instead, she forces them to wrestle their inner demons, with all the brutality and desperation that hand to hand combat entails. <br /><br />Which brings me to Froi. (<i>Froi!</i>) For those who have read Finnikin of the Rock, you’ll be aware of the fact that Froi attempts something abhorrent in the first book. So it speaks to Marchetta’s skill as a writer that she is able to develop this character - his shame, his humanity, his convictions - in such a way that makes him deeply compelling. There are plenty of easy roads Marchetta could have taken in bringing Froi back as a main character, effectively glossing over his backstory. But I think that would have taken away from the thematic power of the novel, and been disingenuous to the character himself. Instead, by exploring the darker side of Froi’s nature, she creates a character so conflicted, and so authentic, it actually makes me ache. <br /> <br /><i>”Although a voice inside had chanted to stop that night, Froi would never know if he would have. And he wanted to know. He wanted to say the words, ‘I would not have gone through with it.’ But he’d never know and that was his punishment.”</i><br /> <br />That passage punches me in the gut every time, and it’s small moments of crystallised thought such as this that make Froi’s growth throughout the novel, redefining the terms on which he lives his life, so real and heartbreaking. <br /> <br />But it’s not only Froi that Marchetta is unafraid of putting into morally ambiguous and unsympathetic positions, flaws exposed. Almost every character in the novel has to fight for something, has some excruciating internal journey to travel. Lucian, Beatriss, Trevanion, Lirah, Gargarin, amongst others – all carry with them some kind of pain, and have been or must go through something that will alter them irrevocably. While not always (if at all) providing tidy resolutions, there’s something rewarding about accompanying these characters on their journeys. There is a redemptive nature to their growth, and an acknowledgement that people are rarely all good or all evil, and all are capable of both inflicting pain.<br /> <br />And then, Quintana. Oh, Quintana. I’m not sure there is a character I’ve felt so fiercely about recently. She is my spirit animal. Neither clichéd fantasy princess or “kickass heroine” in a physical sense, Quintana is an alloy of contradictions: vulnerability, humour, grief, rage, intelligence, insanity. She’s tenacious and a little bit feral. She’s passionate and cold. And though this is largely Froi’s story, the chemistry of these two characters, the way they crash together on the page, is pretty captivating. <br /><br />I won’t brush off the fact that this isn’t a light book, in terms of the content. Be warned that there’s all manner of brutality in this story: rape, torture, infanticide – Marchetta takes Froi of the Exiles to some very dark places. Reader thresholds for this type of subject matter will vary, naturally, but I feel it’s worth mentioning that it didn’t read gratuitously to me. The inclusion felt purposeful, important to the story being told. <br /><br />On the other hand, it would remiss of me not to note that this book worthwhile things to say on the issues of religious tolerance, racism and cultural prejudice. Just as she does not flinch from showing both the repugnant and the admirable in her characters, Marchetta also shows the cruelty humans are capable of, along with their capacity for forgiveness and absolution. <br /><br />Underpinning this very involved and intense novel, however, is the very human desire to belong somewhere. To have a sense of home, of family, and connection. And that this can sometimes be found in the most unlikely of places. <br /><br /><b>tl;dr:</b> This book is a beautifully complex, emotional wrecking ball. It’s brilliant. <br /><br />P.S. Thank goodness I held off from reading this until now. I think a year long wait for Quintana of Charyn might have completely cracked me. <br /><br />* * * * *<br />I can't even, people. I just finished and everything hurts.<br /><br />::<strong>SHOULDERS</strong>::<br /><br />Readalong with the delightful Emily :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="303428876887408215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_207570644" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/207570644" />
    <a title="Maggie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222084-maggie"><img alt="Maggie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319666686p2/4222084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/207570644?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie" href="/user/show/4222084-maggie">Maggie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=i-ve-just-read-you-and-i-love-you">i-ve-just-read-you-and-i-love-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=crushworthy-guys">crushworthy-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=aussie-aussie-aussie-oi-oi-oi">aussie-aussie-aussie-oi-oi-oi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222084-maggie?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer207570644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8067303926399359704">Reviewing a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta' title='Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melina Marchetta</a> book always takes me longer than reading one, even a 600-page whopper like <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_' title='Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Froi of the Exiles</a>
</i>. It's like this: If someone were to point to this pen<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358749i/709900.png' width='496' height='131' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>and ask, "What color is this?", the answer is easy.<br/><br/>Blue.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380358749ra/709901.gif' width='500' height='230' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>But if the person pointed to a rainbow and asked, "What color is this?", the answer is no longer simple because a rainbow is every color. Likewise, a Marchetta book can't be narrowed down to one thing or one emotion. It's every emotion.<br/><br/>In <i>Froi of the Exiles</i>, as in</span>
  <span id="freeText8067303926399359704" style="display:none">Reviewing a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta" title="Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Melina Marchetta</a> book always takes me longer than reading one, even a 600-page whopper like <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a>
</i>. It's like this: If someone were to point to this pen<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358749i/709900.png" width="496" height="131" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>and ask, "What color is this?", the answer is easy.<br><br>Blue.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380358749ra/709901.gif" width="500" height="230" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But if the person pointed to a rainbow and asked, "What color is this?", the answer is no longer simple because a rainbow is every color. Likewise, a Marchetta book can't be narrowed down to one thing or one emotion. It's every emotion.<br><br>In <i>Froi of the Exiles</i>, as in <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4932435.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles___1_" title="Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles, #1) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Finnikin of the Rock</a>
</i>, Marchetta shows the devastating effects of war, both internal and external, on people and on nations. But, despite the topic, her books aren't about devastation. They're about hope. They're about people. Marchetta finds the humanity in people deemed unworthy by other members of society, me included. The Froi I first met in <i>Finnikin</i>? Had it been up to me, he would be rotting somewhere in Sorel. Instead Marchetta refused to give up on Froi or on me and trusted that we'd learn and grow. Now he's the titular character and deservedly so because Froi's journey into Charyn is as complex and surprising as Froi himself. <br><br>As she did in <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7417780.The_Piper_s_Son" title="The Piper's Son by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">The Piper's Son</a>
</i>, Marchetta introduces a new cast of characters to surround the supporting-turned-lead actor. And like in <i>Piper</i>, I found myself wondering, How does she DO that?? With <i>Froi</i>, Marchetta got me MORE invested in the story, gave me MORE characters to love, and found MORE ways to break my heart. And while introducing us to Quintana, Gargarin, Lirah, and the people of Charyn, she doesn't forget about Finnikin, Trevanion, Beatriss and the people of Lumatere. Then, because that's not enough, there's the storyline involving Lucian of Lumatere and Phaedra of Charyn. It sounds like a lot, and it is, but it's not more than you can handle. If anything, you want MORE.<br><br>I'm being purposefully vague in my review because there's no way I can lay out this story better than Marchetta. If you've never read any of her books, there's a reason why people pay double the price of a US book to have her books shipped from Australia. Or, like me, they buy both the Australian and US editions. And ebook. And audiobook. I put my money where my mouth is when I tell you she is worth every penny. (Speaking of audiobooks, I've been listening to the audio version of <i>Finnikin</i> and Charyn is pronounced Sha-RIN, not CHAIR-in, which is what I'd been saying.)<br><br>One thing about Marchetta that I think is often overlooked because she brings so much to the table is how funny she is. I laughed as much as I cried while reading <i>Froi</i>. Froi is a smartass to begin with, and combined with the grumpy old men and coddled manchildren of Charyn, there were scenes that had me laughing out loud. <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156897537" rel="nofollow noopener">Catie</a> is great at choosing the perfect song for a book. I'm better with movies. With Froi -- damaged, destructive, hopeful, wonderful Froi -- I kept being reminded of something Ethan Hawke as Troy said in <i>Reality Bites</i>:<br><i>
  <blockquote>You can't navigate me. I may do mean things, and I may hurt you, and I may run away without your permission, and you may hate me forever, and I know that scares the living shit outta you 'cause you know I'm the only real thing you got.</blockquote>
</i><br>And Melina Marchetta: <i>I love her. She breaks my heart again and again, but I love her.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8067303926399359704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
